Beijing-Shanghai Train Accident Repaired Yesterday

Passengers and staff were unharmed.

The railway bureau suffered losses of 100,000.

Trains will operate as usual today.

Details of the accident that occurred on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway involving the 20th third- and fourth-class slow train from Beijing to Shanghai between Huangdu and Anting last night were reported briefly in yesterday's newspaper. The following is a more detailed account of the situation at the time and the status of train operations yesterday.

Details of the accident: The train was originally scheduled to arrive at Shanghai North Station at 8:45 PM, but was delayed by more than two hours. There was no prior warning, which led to the disaster. The accident site was at the beginning of the 26th kilometer, near Bridge No. 24, not far from Huangdu Station. There were patrol guards stationed there, and military barracks were built, but the bandits managed to achieve their destructive goals, which was quite unexpected. On both sides of the tracks, the bandits pried off screws.

Rescue vehicle uses crane to lift the train

(Special correspondent from this newspaper photographed)

Six screws were removed, and four fishplates connecting the two rails were also removed. As a result, when the train passed through the area, the locomotive managed to get through because of its greater power, but the iron shed guard car, a 40-ton shed car, four fourth-class passenger cars, and two third-class passenger cars behind it all derailed due to the rails loosening outward, and tilted slightly outward. Fortunately, the driver noticed early and immediately stopped the train, so the last five passenger cars did not derail. The passengers in the derailed cars were in the process of organizing their belongings as they were about to arrive in Shanghai when they suddenly heard a loud noise and saw the cars tilting outward, as if they were about to fall. They were greatly alarmed, and the order was extremely chaotic. The guard of the rear car learned that there was danger ahead, immediately jumped off the train, and rushed to Huangdu Station to report and request assistance. He also tried to help the passengers out of the derailed cars and into the rear cars. Shanghai North Station immediately sent telegrams to the relevant officials to come to the station to provide assistance. However, it was already midnight, and the craftsmen had dispersed, so the rescue train could not be dispatched immediately. It was not until 8:00 AM yesterday morning that the craftsmen arrived, totaling more than 100 people. They were led by the chief of the locomotive department and traveled to the scene of the accident on the rescue train. A separate empty train was sent to pick up the passengers and bring them to Shanghai.

Rescue situation: When the rescue train arrived at the scene of the accident, the damaged tracks were completely removed, and new tracks and sleepers were laid. The guard car, the 40-ton shed car, and the No. 612 fourth-class car, which were less damaged, were placed on the rails first. There were still three fourth-class cars, Nos. 805, 901, and 902, and two third-class cars, Nos. 79 and 84, that were leaning too much and could not be lifted by hooks. Liquid oxygen was used to burn off the hooks, and then cranes were used to lift them one at a time onto the rails. The craftsmen worked tirelessly from morning to evening, and the damaged vehicles were repaired and sent to the Zhabei Factory for repair at 7:00 PM last night.

Train operations: After learning of the accident, Shanghai North Station urgently telegraphed Nanxiang to stop the special express train from Shanghai to Beijing, which had already departed, and ordered the original train to return to the North Station. All passengers were allowed to refund their tickets at the original price. The upward intercity trains from Shanghai to Wuxi, Changzhou, Kunshan, and Anting, and the downward intercity trains from Changshu, Wuxi, Kunshan, and Anting to Shanghai were temporarily suspended. However, through trains between Beijing and Shanghai and between Beijing and Hangzhou continued to operate as usual. However, passengers had to get off the train at the accident site and walk dozens of yards before transferring to another train to reach their destination. Therefore, the schedules of all trains yesterday were unpredictable. Passengers were only allowed to carry light luggage. Last night, the No. 10 express train from Shanghai to Hangzhou, which was originally scheduled to depart at 5:50 PM, was delayed until after 9:00 PM due to waiting for passengers on the Beijing-Shanghai through train. The special express trains from Shanghai to Beijing and from Beijing to Shanghai, which departed at 11:00 PM last night, added an extra train due to overcrowding. Trains will operate as usual from today.

Loss situation: According to a post-accident investigation, no passengers or train staff were injured, and no items were lost. However, the losses in terms of vehicles and materials were considerable, estimated at around 100,000 yuan. The Railway Bureau has reported this to the Ministry of Railways and has strictly ordered the police along the route to increase patrols to ensure the safety of travelers.

Banking Industry Discussing Consolidation of Internal Debt

The Banking Association Initiates a Creditors' Group

Banking Industries in Pingjin Send Representatives to Participate

National Creditors Will Register

Riri News reports that the Ministry of Finance has been holding meetings in Beijing for days regarding the consolidation of foreign debt, but plans for internal debt consolidation have not yet been discussed. The banking industry in this port believes that with the domestic war pacified and domestic products now able to flow freely, the revitalization of industry and the development of the national economy are imminent. However, the amount of internal debt is very large and urgently needs to be consolidated to establish a foundation for revitalizing industrial capital. Therefore, at noon the day before yesterday, the Shanghai Banking Association convened Zhang Gongquan, President of the Bank of China, Hu Mengjia, Manager of the Bank of Communications, Xiao Fuxiao, Manager of the Continental Bank, Wu Yunzhai, Manager of the Jincheng Bank, Chen Zheqing, Manager of the Yanyeh Bank, and Li Fuxun, Chairman of the Bank of China, at the Banking Association at No. 4 Hong Kong Road to discuss the matter. It was agreed that internal debt consolidation should not be delayed and that a creditors' group should be established to request the Ministry of Finance to begin consolidation in the near future. However, the specific consolidation plan should be determined by the Banking Association convening the Shanghai banking community to form a creditors' group for the banking portion of Chinese internal debt. A telegram was sent to the Banking Associations of Beiping and Tianjin seeking their agreement to send representatives to Shanghai for a meeting at a fixed date. Other banking communities in other ports were not notified due to the lack of internal debt relationships. After the establishment of the bank internal debt creditors' group, a report will be submitted to solicit creditors across the country to register internal debt. At 7 PM last night, the Beiping Banking Association sent a reply expressing its support and appointed Tan Danya, President of the Continental Bank of Shanghai, and Zhou Zuomin, President of the Jincheng Bank, as representatives of the Beiping Banking Association. However, the date of the formal meeting has not yet been set. The total amount of foreign debt is approximately 130 million yuan in national currency, of which internal debt accounts for three-tenths and strong foreign debt accounts for seven-tenths and is weak. Although a plan for foreign debt consolidation has been drafted, it has not yet been announced. It is roughly based on a certain item of national fiscal revenue as the basis for foreign debt settlement, and it is expected that internal debt can be fully repaid within 30 years, and China's economic position in the international community can also be independent.

Central Temporary Coupon Holders Association Submits Document to Chairman Chiang

Requesting Immediate Recall and Full Redemption: Yesterday, the United Association of Holders of Central Bank Temporary Exchange Coupons submitted a document to Chiang Kai-shek, Chairman of the National Government, stating that the Central Bank's temporary exchange coupons had been delayed in redemption, causing immense suffering, and requesting sympathy and immediate authorization for full redemption to alleviate commercial difficulties and benefit the people. The Central Bank temporary exchange coupons were issued on August 26, 1926, with the approval of the National Government when you, Mr. Chairman, were serving as Commander-in-Chief of the National Revolutionary Army, and were entrusted to the General Headquarters Political Affairs Bureau and Treasury. The coupon amount was five million silver dollars, with denominations of one yuan, five yuan, and ten yuan. The coupons were stamped with the seal of the General Headquarters Political Affairs Bureau and the official seals of the Treasury Director, and the issuance regulations were formulated and promulgated by the General Headquarters, and a notice was issued to inform merchants and the public to accept and use them equally and fully, without any delay or negligence. The National Revolutionary Army fought for principles and worked hard for the nation and the people. The righteous army was welcomed everywhere by the masses, and the army traveled thousands of miles with great hardship and meritorious achievements shining like the sun and the moon. The people looked up to the grand plans and unanimously expressed their gratitude and support. No one in history has gained the hearts of the people as much as you, Mr. Chairman. The people's faith in you, Mr. Chairman, was so strong, and their enthusiasm for welcoming the Revolutionary Army was so great that they all accepted and used these Central Bank temporary exchange coupons, which contributed greatly to the Northern Expedition military campaign. You, Mr. Chairman, are wise and intelligent and will not disregard this fact. However, for some unknown reason, the coupons suddenly stopped being redeemed later, causing panic and distress among merchants holding the coupons, who ran around in a state of shock and anxiety, repeatedly appealing without being approved for the past four years, suffering considerable losses. You, Mr. Chairman, have been deeply concerned and caring for the people, and we trust that you have seen all this suffering. Now that the Yan-Feng warlords have completely collapsed, the reactionary forces have been almost completely wiped out, the country is unified, the foundation is solid, and national and public welfare are flourishing. You, Mr. Chairman, have been working hard to follow the teachings of the late Premier and to respond to the national sentiment of the people, and you have been working diligently to promote good governance, remove the old and establish the new, and start anew with the people. All domestic and foreign public debts have been consolidated, and the country's prestige is growing day by day, and the revitalization of the people's livelihood is imminent. Since the Central Bank temporary exchange coupons are related to the revolution and their nature is different from internal debt, they cannot be compared with other internal debts. Moreover, during the Northern Expedition military campaign, the Central Bank Ocean Coupons for the three provinces of Hubei, Hunan, and Jiangxi, the Small Ocean Coupons for the three provinces of Hunan, Jiangxi, and Guangxi, and the Hankou banknotes of the Central Bank, which were issued after the Central Temporary Exchange Coupons, have all been consolidated and closed. Why have you delayed the consolidation of the Central Temporary Exchange Coupons? This seems unfair and does not accord with the way to love the people. Merchants are deeply concerned and have no choice but to petition you, Mr. Chairman, to consider the difficulties of merchants and the plight of the people, and to grant an order to the Ministry of Finance to immediately recall and fully redeem the Central Bank temporary exchange coupons to alleviate commercial difficulties and benefit the people. We are extremely grateful and pray to you with tears in our eyes.

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Consolidates Branches

Yesterday, the second board meeting passed several consolidation plans. Li Zhonggong, Commissioner of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, believed that since the company has been nationalized, all organizational methods should undergo fundamental reform. Yesterday, he convened the second board meeting at the company to discuss consolidation plans. Those in attendance included Song Shuqiao, Secretary-General of the company, Chen Zhitin, Yu Zhiming, Zhou Shian, Huang Penghao, Kong Xiangrong, Fu Jucun, Lu Qinghai, and Shen Zhongyi, Secretaries, Sun Jingxiang, Manager of the Four Branches, Cao Zijia, Wang Renjing, He Molin, and Wang Chengxiong, Deputy Section Chiefs, and Li Gufan and Li Ruomei, Deputy Chairmen and Committee Members of the Regulations Committee. Li Zhonggong chaired the meeting, Zhou Shian and Li Ruomei took notes. Many resolutions were discussed and passed. The important ones are as follows: Matters submitted by the Commissioner: (1) The Organizational Regulations of the General Management Office were generally approved after being explained by Song Shuqiao, Chairman of the Regulations Committee. The chiefs of each section and the chairmen and vice-chairmen of the Regulations Committee were designated to review the textual omissions. (2) Consolidation plan of each branch: It was resolved that (A) the administrative and personnel powers of each branch should be centralized in the General Office; (B) the application and distribution of bonuses should be regulated so that bonuses should be distributed universally among all branches of the General Office in order to ensure fairness; (C) in principle, the Shanghai branch should be separated according to the Business Section, and the Business Section should prepare a comparative description of the advantages and disadvantages of the separation, which should be approved by the Commissioner; (D) the revision plan for each branch and agency, the decision on the actual reporting and actual sales system and the contract payment system, and the revision of the business ratio and expenditure budget should all be planned by the Design Committee and approved by the Commissioner. (3) Establishing each wheel industry supervision case was resolved and passed. The business service rules were handed over to the Rules and Regulations Committee for drafting. (4) The Business Section proposed that the National Government order the Ministry of Railways to instruct the Railway Administration to coordinate the water and land joint transport method, and the case of changing the cabin positions of the Guangda and Guangli wheels to facilitate loading of goods was passed. (5) The staff condolence rules proposed jointly by the Secretariat and the Business Section and the proposal on the crew service regulations proposed by the Ship Affairs Section were handed over to the Rules and Regulations Committee for handling. (6) It was passed that all company documents should be written in Chinese. (7) The Ship Affairs Section should prepare a plan for the supplementary training of driving wheel engine business personnel for approval. (8) Shen Section Chief proposed that the affairs of the Shashi and Yichang bureaus should be handled separately by one person to meet the needs. It was resolved that the Shashi business should be temporarily assigned by the Yichang Bureau to another person to manage. There were many other proposals, which are not listed in detail. The meeting concluded at seven o'clock.

Wenzhou Donation Storm Affects Shanghai Shipping and Freight

Dockworkers have gone on strike, and freight transport has been blocked and delayed. It is feared that this will lead to a strike in the city. In Wenzhou, merchants are protesting against the increase in taxes on foreign and Cantonese goods, leading to a freight strike. The two sides are not giving way to each other, causing the turmoil to escalate, and Shanghai's commerce and shipping have also suffered significant losses. The following is a more detailed report on the matter:

The foreign and Cantonese goods tax was changed to unified donation: On the 16th of this month, the Wenzhou Foreign and Cantonese Goods Tax Donation Bureau was ordered to merge into the Yongjia Unified Donation Bureau. After the bureau took over the foreign and Cantonese goods tax affairs, it announced that from the 17th, the Wenzhou Foreign and Cantonese Goods Donation would change its method, abolishing the old rules and changing to unified donation collection. The tax amount would be notified by the bureau to the foreign and Cantonese goods industry and merchants. Upon receiving the news, the foreign and Cantonese goods industry considered that the foreign and Cantonese goods tax was light, and the unified donation tax was heavy. Once the merchants agreed to pay, their burden would increase by 20% to 30%. As a result, the industry convened its members and unanimously opposed the change, requesting that the original system not be changed. As a result, the donation bureau also announced that the unified tax on non-foreign and Cantonese goods would be increased at the same time. The business community faced these two waves of unrest at the same time, leading to the boycott of strikes and other actions.

Page 14

Strikes and boycotts by various industries: From the 17th, the allocation and export of goods in the foreign and Cantonese goods industry was the first to be suspended. On the 18th, because the tax bureau still insisted on the original proposal and refused to compromise, other industries also joined the strike unanimously. A group was organized to request exemption from the tax increase, fearing that one or two treacherous merchants would privately transport goods. Therefore, dockworkers and stevedores at each wharf were ordered to go on strike from the 17th, so that goods could not be loaded or unloaded. Transportation to and from Wenzhou was completely cut off.

The unrest is growing: From the 18th, commercial representatives held a meeting at the Chamber of Commerce for two days, hoping that the tax bureau would stop changing the unified donation and increasing the tax rate, but the tax bureau did not agree to the repeated requests. According to a telegram from Wenzhou yesterday, the situation of the businesses has gradually deteriorated, and the crisis of a city-wide strike is imminent.

Problems with Shanghai goods: The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Guangji ship returned to Shanghai empty yesterday, using 35 tons of mud and sand to balance the ship. The problem of outbound goods after arriving in Shanghai has not yet been determined. Because foreign and Cantonese goods cannot be loaded, it is not certain whether other goods can be transported. The port workers have gone on strike, and if this problem is not resolved, it is feared that the goods cannot be unloaded. Therefore, whether to load outbound goods on the Guangji ship must wait for a telegram from Wenzhou. However, because the sailing is on schedule, the ship must leave.

Considerable losses to Shanghai ships: As the end of the year approaches, Wenzhou freight is rushing to load. Suddenly, a freight strike has occurred for many days. Three ships from Shanghai to Wenzhou, Guangji, Haiyan, and Yili, and four motor sailboats are currently returning to Shanghai empty due to lack of goods to load. The Guangji has lost more than 2,000 taels in freight by not transporting goods. The Haiyan ship will also return empty to Shanghai. The losses caused by the suspension of sailboats due to lack of goods to load are also huge. Shanghai merchants who have booked goods in Wenzhou waiting to be transported to Shanghai are even more anxious, and those who inquire at the shipping companies are coming in droves.

Navy Implements Escort Service for Yangtze River Shipping

Pirate activity is rampant along the upper reaches of the Yangtze River. Foreign merchants have already dispatched troops to protect their ships. Chinese river steamers, concerned about business and passenger safety, have also requested the government to send warships to patrol the area. This matter was previously reported in this newspaper, and further updates are reported as follows:

The British steamer Qizhou encountered danger. The Taikoo company's Yangtze River steamers Datong, Anqing, and others, en route from the Yangtze to Shanghai, encountered a pirate attack near Qizhou. The pirates first fired warning shots, then opened fire on the two steamers with six cannon shots. Two shells landed just outside the Anqing's outer barricade, a very close call. The British navy personnel on board returned fire with eight shells towards the pirates on the riverbank, and the pirates fled. Navigation remains extremely dangerous between Jiujiang and Huangzhou. Ships are reportedly navigating at night with their lights off.

The Navy Dispatches Warships for Escort Duty. Shanghai shipping merchants telegraphed headquarters requesting the dispatch of naval warships to protect merchant ships on the upper Yangtze bound for Yichang, Changsha, and Xiangtan. Headquarters has replied to Shanghai stating that two warships have been dispatched to the Chengling and Jianli area to suppress bandits and provide escort. Consequently, starting from the 20th, Yangtze steamers traveling from Hankou to Yichang, such as those belonging to China Merchants and Sanbei companies, are being escorted by the Chengsheng warship. However, pirate activity was again discovered near Jianli yesterday. Downbound merchant ships have stopped operating for fear of travel. After sending a telegram requesting assistance, the Ministry of the Navy has ordered the Jiangkun warship stationed in the Yuezhou area to urgently suppress the bandits and protect the ships to Hankou.

New Marker Buoys Installed in Xinzhou. The shoals and reefs near Huoyanshan, above Jiujiang, are constantly shifting. Navigation is especially dangerous during the low water season, and even slight carelessness can lead to grounding and accidents. Yesterday, the Jianghan Customs notified Shanghai shipping companies that marker buoys have been placed at the most dangerous shoals and reefs in Xinzhou, serving as navigational aids for upbound and downbound Yangtze steamers. Yangtze ships passing through the area must adhere to the warning lights, maintaining a distance of five English miles to avoid accidents in shallow waters. Indeed, these matters are perilous.

The Congestion of Vessels Due to Shallow Waters in the Wusong River is Cleared

Fan Hesheng, chairman of the Shanghai Municipal Rice Merchants Association, reported that at 3:00 PM on the 19th of this month, the narrowness of the Yujidun River combined with shallow autumn waters caused a sudden congestion of arriving ships. Four security guards from the association, along with Meng and Wang, the two patrol chiefs of the Sixth District, First Precinct of the Water Police, led the water police in efforts to clear the congestion. By 6:00 PM, normal passage had resumed. According to a report from the association's security guards, the situation has returned to normal.

Municipal Government Promotes the New System of Weights and Measures

Promulgation of Uniform Standards for Public Weights and Measures in the Municipality. The municipal government considers the promotion of the new system of weights and measures to be a crucial task. Shanghai, being a major port for trade, is under international scrutiny and should actively work to complete the standardization as scheduled. Eight articles of the proposed Shanghai Municipal Uniform Standards for Public Weights and Measures have been drafted, promulgated, and are now in effect. The original text of the articles are excerpted below:

Article 1: These regulations apply to all levels of central or local government agencies within the city of Shanghai.

Article 2: December 31, Year 19 (of the Republic), is declared as the date for the unification of public weights and measures within the city.

Article 3: From the date of promulgation of these regulations, all documents and records related to weights and measures in all agencies shall uniformly adhere to the standard system.

Article 4: From the date of promulgation of these regulations, all agencies shall immediately cease procuring equipment based on the old system. Existing equipment must be submitted to the Municipal Bureau of Weights and Measures for inspection and registration by November 30, Year 19. However, if there is an excessive amount of equipment that is inconvenient to move, the bureau may be notified to send personnel to conduct the inspection on-site.

Article 5: From the date of promulgation of these regulations, all public documents and other files submitted by the public to government agencies involving weights and measures shall uniformly adhere to the standard system.

Article 6: From the day after the declaration of unification, old system weights and measures equipment in all agencies shall be uniformly converted using the new system.

Article 7: These regulations may be amended at any time if there are any omissions.

Article 8: These regulations shall come into effect on the date of promulgation by the Municipal Government.

Zhejiang Farmers Oppose the Sale of Japanese Autumn Cocoons in Shanghai

The Preparatory Office of the Zhejiang Cocoon Industry Association Federation received a joint letter yesterday from farmers Zhang Tianshou and others from Jiaxing and other counties stating: We recently heard that a large quantity of Japanese autumn cocoons have arrived in Shanghai and are being peddled everywhere by brokers. Those who are ignorant are inevitably tempted by profit and forget righteousness. Although various sectors have loudly protested against the import of Japanese cocoons, the Shanghai Silk and Cocoon General Association, which is insane and out of control, has requested a reduction in import duties, resulting in a continuous influx into China. In this situation, the General Association is the sole entity that is controlling the lives of our farmers. We vow to devise appropriate countermeasures. On one hand, we urge your association to pay attention to this import of autumn cocoons. If any silk mills in Shanghai purchase these cocoons, we hope that you will secretly investigate and report to the inland farmers' associations. When those mills go inland to purchase cocoons next year, we will devise appropriate measures to resist them. We are anxiously awaiting orders. Signed, Zhang Tianshou, Wang Ziming, Qian Dasheng, Wang Qiang, Zhou Shaozhai, and 1,512 farmers from Jiaxing, Jiashan, Tongxiang, and Haiyan counties.

Pawn Industry Demands Revision of Labor Conditions

The employer representatives have scheduled a meeting on the 28th to discuss the conditions of employment in the local pawn industry. The employees of the pawn industry, noting that the former compensation and working condition terms have not been conscientiously followed by the management side, have therefore passed a measure proposing 17 changes to the original terms, among which the most important is #2 (compensation): the terms of the positions will be uniformly: manager 20 yuan per ‘bao’ (package), package supervisor 19.50 yuan, gold decorations 19 yuan, head counter 18.50 yuan, second counter 18 yuan, second counter 17.50 yuan, book keeping 17 yuan, wrapping packages 16 yuan, clearing tickets 15 yuan, tag hanging 14 yuan, apprentice year 1 (13 yuan), apprentice year 2 (12 yuan), apprentice year 3 (11 yuan), apprentice year 4 (10 yuan), apprentice year 5 (9 yuan), apprentice year 6 (8 yuan). All administration 10 yuan. A double month’s pay is given in the twelfth month. #9 (layoff): if the pawn shop owner closes his shop due to unforeseen circumstances, the owners must disburse 300 yuan as layoff compensation. The compensation will be paid according to the existing market value, and before the settlement is resolved, the employers will disburse the double month’s pay. At one point, the employees negotiated directly with the management side, but due to the management representatives failing to show up to a negotiation meeting the meeting could not proceed. Therefore the employees are imploring a higher level of mediation. The Social Affairs Bureau, therefore, will summon on the 20th a conversation between management and labor to work together and attempt to reach a new consensus. It was noted that if after two weeks there is no fruit, then the bureau will intercede. The employer organizations (Special District Pawn Industry Association) and (Pawn Industry Association) have scheduled a meeting to take place on November 28th to discuss the situation.

Aid Society for the Ding-Huang Tragedy Established by Various Sectors in Xuhui

The Fifth Precinct of the Ninth District Sends a Telegram Seeking Assistance. Various sectors in Xuhui, in response to the tragedy caused by French sailors' drunken assault on our countrymen Ding Jiaqun and Huang Haiyou (details reported in the newspapers on the 14th), resulting in Ding Jiaqun being blinded, formed a support association. They believe that if no assistance is provided and no negotiations are conducted, it will be impossible to prevent future incidents and avenge this humiliation. Therefore, a support meeting was held at the Ninth District Party Headquarters at 2:00 PM on the 20th of this month. Representatives from various sectors attended, including Shen Shuowen from the Ninth District Party Headquarters, Zhu Shiqi and Liu Rong from the Ninth District Eleventh Precinct, Chen Yunlan from the Ninth District Second Precinct, Chen Xiaomei from the Ninth District First Precinct, Fu Huaichen from the Wuzhou Workers' Association, He Lianzhou and Gu Jinqing from the Huxi Construction Workers' Union, Sun Hongfei from the Tenth Team of the Hunan Security Corps, Fan Yuanlong, Lin Diangang, and Luo Jinbao from the Jiangsu Yanfu Sojourners Association in Shanghai, Zhuang Yaoming from the Eighth Village Farmers' Association, and Liu Yunfang from the Sixth District Second Station, totaling over fifty people. Zhu Shiqi was elected as the chairman and Chen Xiaomei as the secretary. The chairman reported on the incident, recounting the barbaric and unreasonable behavior of the French soldiers stationed in the occupied territories, who have been wantonly bullying our countrymen, leading to this tragedy. He stated that if serious negotiations are not conducted, it will be impossible to prevent future incidents. All our compatriots should fight for justice to achieve ultimate victory. Liu Yunfang, chief of the Sixth District Second Station, then reported on the details of the incident. After that, the discussion focused on the measures to be taken: (1) It was decided that the name of the organization should be the Xuhui Aid Society for the Ding-Huang Tragedy. (2) It was decided to send representatives to express condolences to the victims. Zhu Shiqi and Chen Xiaomei were chosen to go. (3) It was decided that the Jiangsu Yancheng/Fugou Sojourners Association in Shanghai will be responsible for economic organisation. (4) It was decided to request the higher authorities to (1) withdraw the French soldiers stationed in the occupied territories (2) punish the perpetrators (3) provide compensation (4) issue an apology and guarantee that they will not station in occupied territories again in the future. (5) It was decided to elect representatives to conduct the negotiations, including Zhu Shiqi from the Eleventh Precinct, Luo Jinbao from the Jiangsu Yanfu Sojourners Association, Fu Huaichen from the Wuzhou Workers' Association, Chen Yunlan from the Second Precinct, Hong Sunfei from the Security Corps, and He Lianzhou from the Huxi Construction Workers' Union. (6) It was decided to submit a report to the municipal department for record. (7) It was decided to ask Shen Shuowen to assist with the documents of the association. (8) It was decided that the next meeting would be convened by the Jiangsu Yanfu Sojourners Association when necessary. The meeting concluded as the clock struck seven.

The Fifth Precinct of the Ninth District Sends a Telegram: To all newspapers, French organizations, and compatriots throughout the country: The French imperialist soldiers stationed in the occupied territories of Xujiahui have always been extremely vicious. There is no longer any regard for our Chinese people. Rape of women and drunken assaults causing injuries have occurred repeatedly. On the evening of the 8th of this month, at 9:00 PM, a group of French soldiers, while drunk, committed a heinous crime, injuring two people severely and three people slightly. Their lives are now in imminent danger. Hearing this news, we are filled with outrage. The French imperialists are treating human lives as worthless and disgracing our nation. It is unbearable. We earnestly hope that people from all walks of life will rise up together to protect our national rights and prevent aggression. This urgent telegram expresses our utmost indignation. Shanghai Special City Party Department, Fifth Precinct of the Ninth District.

Two Medical Associations Approved to Establish Separately

The Order of the Municipal Citizen Training Council. The Public Training Council of the Shanghai Municipal Party Department yesterday ordered the Chinese Medical Association and the Shenzhou Medical Association, stating: In order to comply with orders, this Council previously ordered the association to stop activity due to its strange naming convention and organization, and to merge into the Chinese Medicine Association. However, this association had a defense in which it claimed its organization was purely academic, purposed to research academia, ameliorate medicine, auxiliary administration, and enlightened sanitation. A review of the functions of both organizations show that they are very different. We implore for maintenance of the establishment and withdraw prior decisions. However, a review shows that the association has yet to fully receive permit procedures. Therefore the order will ask the association to comply with social organization rules and to confirm the associations’ name and purpose with the Council. We will also ask that they are confirmed to academic research, regarding the membership that guarantees the opening and settlement of business dispute, that they will be administered into the Chinese Medicine Association, and that the association will not intervene. Finally, we ask the association to focus on academy and to cease any other actions to influence other sectors that would affect the progress of the people.

Implementation of Inspection of Imported Sugar

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the Sugar Merchants Association yesterday regarding the inspection of imported sugar, stating: We are writing to inform you that on the 20th of this month, we received Instruction No. 13812 from the Ministry of Industry and Commerce regarding the inspection of sugar. The instruction stated that imported sugar from foreign countries is a major commodity and a food product that is easily counterfeited, making it necessary to implement inspections. In light of this, the Ministry has formulated and promulgated the "Regulations for Inspection of Imported Sugar," consisting of fourteen articles, which will take effect on November 15th of this year. In addition to instructing the Commodity Inspection Bureaus of Shanghai, Hankou, Tianjin, Qingdao, and Guangzhou to conduct inspections on a regular basis, we are also sending this instruction for your information. We are enclosing a copy of the "Regulations for Inspection of Imported Sugar" for your reference. This letter is addressed to the Shanghai Municipal Sugar Merchants Association.

The Red Cross Receives the Latest Disaster Report from Henan

Chenliu, Tongxu, and Kaocheng people urgently await relief to alleviate their misery. The Chinese Red Cross Society yesterday received three telegrams from Chairman Zhang Fang of the Henan Relief Committee reporting the unbearable disaster situation in Chenliu, Tongxu, and Kaocheng counties. It is hoped that those who are concerned about relief efforts will take immediate action. (1) The Chinese Red Cross Society: According to a report from the War Disaster Investigation Committee of the subordinate association, Ren Huanxin, and the Chenliu County Magistrate Xu Futian, the war caused 7,000 people in the county to be killed, wounded, or displaced, with their whereabouts unknown. Over 4,300 large carts and 11,000 cattle and horses were lost. Levies were imposed seven times, totaling over 360,000 yuan. Grain and forage were requisitioned, valued at over 210,000 yuan. War trenches were dug, destroying 16,000 zhang of farmland, each over one zhang deep and wide. Countless houses were destroyed and possessions looted. Now that the war is over, the affected people have no clothes, food, or livestock. Their lives are in misery. We earnestly request your compassion and grant a large amount of grain and funds to provide relief. Chairman Zhang Fang of the Henan Relief Committee. (2) The Chinese Red Cross Society: According to a report from the Disaster Investigation Committee member Zhang Yuanzong, Tongxu County Magistrate Zhou Gu, the war caused 4,060 people in the county to be killed, wounded, or impressed into military service. Over 1,800 large carts and 6,200 cattle and horses were lost. Military levies were imposed five times, totaling over 47,000 yuan. Grain and forage were requisitioned, valued at approximately 158,000 yuan. War trenches destroyed 39,000 zhang of farmland, passing through 95 villages. Countless houses, trees, clothing, and property were damaged. Now that the war is over, the cries of distress fill the air, and people are desperately awaiting food. It is unbearable to hear. We earnestly request widespread relief. The county is located on a major thoroughfare, and the soil is barren. The wounds of war have not healed from the recent famine. Winter has arrived, and people have no clothes or food. If relief is not provided in advance, people will inevitably perish in ditches. We earnestly request that you quickly allocate grain and funds to provide relief, saving the survivors and rescuing them from disaster. Chairman Zhang Fang of the Henan Relief Committee. (3) The Chinese Red Cross Society: According to a report from the Disaster Investigation Committee members Wang Fangting and Chen Liangfu, Kaocheng County Magistrate Liang Gongyi, Kaocheng County was located on a key war front for over half a year. Over 10,800 people were impressed into military service, killed, wounded, or displaced, with their whereabouts unknown. Over 3,200 houses were burned down. Over 2,200 large carts and 6,600 horses were lost. Levies were imposed totaling over 20,020 yuan. Grain and forage were requisitioned, valued at over 50,040 yuan. Other property losses were estimated at over 100 yuan. War trenches crisscrossed the county, occupying farmland measuring 625,000 chi. These are only the measurable losses, and the indirect damage is incalculable. Winter has arrived, and displaced people are everywhere. We earnestly request relief to save the survivors. The county was located in a war zone that was gained and lost numerous times, causing severe damage to the people. The cold wind is biting, and the huddled figures along the road are pitiful. The hunger fire is burning, and those in the ditches are gasping their last breaths. Now that the war has ended, relief cannot be delayed. We earnestly request that you quickly allocate grain and funds to provide relief, showing humanity and extending the national life. Chairman Zhang Fang of the Henan Relief Committee.

Resolution of Organizational Disputes in the Western Pigment Industry

The Shanghai Municipal Western Pigment Industry Association and the sixteen companies of the Gonghelai Association had a mediation session yesterday afternoon at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce regarding the consolidation issue. The Western Pigment Industry Association was represented by committee members Ma Shangjie, Xi Rungeng, Zhang Jinshou, Zhang Rulin, Yin Runsheng, and Secretary Wang Shipeng. Gonghelai was represented by Shen Jinshen, Zhang Lanping, Li Shuyan, Wang Zuolin, and sixteen other representatives. Zheng Chengqing, a member of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and Chairman Sun Mingqi acted as mediators. The results of the mediation were as follows: (1) All sixteen companies of Gonghelai will merge into the association before November of the lunar calendar. (2) After the merger, a committee will be formed to discuss revisions to the association's charter. (3) A general meeting will be convened to re-elect the association's leadership. The above three items were agreed upon by both parties. The meeting adjourned.

Inspection Report of the Central Bank

The Seventy-Second Report of Inspection of the Central Bank's Issue Reserve stated that the commission, according to the law of the central bank, has the responsibility to inspect the issue of the bank’s convertible note reserve. The Seventy-Second Meeting was held on November 20th to be held at the bank, and has reported results on the inspections. The total amount of convertible notes issued amounts to 21,517,462 yuan, including 2,059,362 yuan in silver dollars and 924,200 yuan in subsidiary coins. The total reserve of convertible notes is 21,917,462 yuan, including 18,764,102 yuan in cash reserve. The cash reserve included 14,056,771.27 yuan stored in the issuing treasury of the bank, 1,268,567 yuan stored in branch bank vaults, and 3,488,762.73 yuan stored in partner vaults. The collateral reserve amounts to 2,753,160 yuan when calculated with silver dollars. According to Article 2, The cash reserve must be 60% and the collateral reserve must be 40%. This inspection has determined that the cash reserve exceeds 60% and the collateral is less than 40%, adhering to code.

The chairman and supervisor of the central bank, Zeng Li, supervisor Wang Jingli, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Ji.

Local News 2

The Realizable Huangpu Iron Bridge

Requiring 5 million in funds, it has been proposed that the government and businessmen cooperate to construct an iron bridge across the Huangpu River in order to develop Pudong's commerce. It is now believed that this plan, which has been in the works for over ten years, will be commenced. According to a reliable investigation by the New Voice Society, the construction of the iron bridge is now actively underway. The most important issue, funding, has now been agreed to by a patron, negating the need to raise funds. The reason why this plan is now deemed to be possible is because the founders Yao Jizhong and Zhao Lanting are both powerful figures. Furthermore, Wang Yiting, Huang Hanzhi, Qu Wenliu, Zhang Xiaoliang, Sheng Maoxiang, Yao Zirang, Yao Ziruo, Gu Xinyi, and Ye Huijun have also strongly endorsed the plan. The reasons and plan have been compiled below.

Reasons: Pudong's land area is greater than the combined areas of the British and French concessions. To the north, the Yangshupu River has depths of several fathoms, and ships of tens of thousands of tons can moor alongside the shore. Therefore, most imported heavy goods are stored in Pudong warehouses. If these goods are to be transported to Puxi, they must undergo the burden of barging, unloading, and loading. In the event of wind and waves, the situation becomes uncontrollable. This is the first reason for the urgent need for this bridge. Although travelers rely on ships to cross the Huangpu River, sudden storms and raging waves often render the boatmen unable to navigate, resulting in frequent capsizings. This is the second reason for the urgent need for this bridge. Pudong's low population density and lack of commercial development require improved transportation to stimulate growth. This is the third reason for the urgent need for this bridge. The basic plan is outlined below:

Funding: The width of the Huangpu River varies. It is proposed to build a steel, movable floating bridge at the narrowest point, south of the large wharf in the South City. The bridge will be approximately 1,800 English feet long. The cost of the bridge foundations, materials, and construction is estimated at 5 million national currency.

Construction: The bridge will be built in the latest European and American style, using pure steel. The form, width, height, and dimensions will be determined by a preparatory committee for the Huangpu Iron Bridge Construction Project, which will be established and staffed by expert engineers.

Nature: The bridge construction costs will be borne by merchants, with the government handling the project. The nature of the project is a public-private partnership.

Management: The government will appoint personnel to jointly organize a bridge management committee with the participating merchants to jointly manage the bridge.

Interest: The project will imitate the road maintenance fees of the Shanghai-Minhang bus company. After the bridge is completed, those who travel across the bridge between Puxi and Pudong will pay a copper coin construction fee to repay the principal and interest. After a certain number of years, the bridge will revert to the government. The above methods will be decided upon by the committee.

Second Kidnapping of a Resident of Duck Nest Sandbar

Bao Shan's wife, recently released by Shen's bandits, was kidnapped again last night by Pan's bandits. Ma Bao Shan and his wife, son of Ma Xing Fan, owner of the Ma Xing Fan fresh fish shop in Duck Nest Sandbar, East Town, Sanjiakou, Wusong, were kidnapped by Shen Guanxi's bandit gang this spring. Details were previously reported in this newspaper. Later, Bao Shan's wife was rescued by her father-in-law and returned home. Bao Shan, however, remained in danger because Shen's bandits demanded too high a ransom. Unexpectedly, at around 8:00 last night, more than ten bandits from Pan Kaiwu's gang, dressed in military uniforms and carrying box cannons and handguns, stormed into the Ma residence to kidnap the owner. Fortunately, Ma Xing Fan heard the noise and, knowing they were bandits, escaped through the back door. The bandits searched the house thoroughly, and when they could not find the owner, they kidnapped Xing Fan's wife, his second son, Bao Shan's wife, the two eldest sons and daughter of Gui Fa, and Bao Shan's young daughter—three generations of mother-in-law, daughter-in-law, and grandchildren, a total of six people, young and old. When the bandits entered the house, they all held a handful of mud and smeared it on the faces of their victims to prevent them from recognizing their faces. Only Gui Fa's wife resisted strongly, angering the bandits, who beat her severely, causing serious injuries. She was not kidnapped, but her life hangs by a thread and may not be saved. A truly tragic event.

### Actress Wang Yanfang Sues Her Teacher for Rape

Learned acting, seduced, and raped, already gave birth to a baby girl. The teacher fled after being accused. The court issued an arrest warrant. The actress Wang Yanfang (real name Ai Lin), 19 years old, from Wuxi, recently had her mother, Wang Zhang, hire lawyer Fei Xizhen at the Special District Court to file a criminal complaint against her teacher, Zhou Wenhui (aka Zhou A'da), accusing him of rape. The complaint stated that the plaintiff had apprenticed to Zhou in July of the 16th year of the Republic to study opera. From October of the 17th year, she performed with the defendant in Wuxi, Changzhou, Jiading, and other places. The defendant, with malicious intent, on the 10th day of the first month of the 18th year of the Republic, when the plaintiff went to Zhou's place for training, lured her into a secret room and used deception and force to rape her, resulting in pregnancy. The plaintiff initially concealed the truth from her mother, but when she went into labor and her abdomen swelled, her mother repeatedly questioned her, forcing her to reveal the details of the rape. She intended to file a complaint immediately, but on the 12th day of the first month of this year, she gave birth to a girl and was physically weak. Fortunately, her parents hired famous doctors to treat her. Now that she has recovered, she is filing a lawsuit, believing that the defendant's rape has ruined her reputation for life, which she cannot bear. According to the law, the defendant has committed the crime of Article 257 of the Criminal Law and should be arrested and severely punished. In addition, she is filing a civil lawsuit, requesting that the court order him to compensate her for the loss of reputation in the amount of 30,000 silver dollars. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Feng Shide opened the court and summoned the defendant, Zhou Wenhui, to appear. Zhou Wenhui did not appear. His mother, Zhou Ye, testified that on December 18th of last year, her son returned from performing in Wuxi with the plaintiff and stayed at the plaintiff's home and never returned home. This time, when the court summoned him, a friend told him that he would be arrested and punished, so he left again and his whereabouts are unknown. The plaintiff, Wang Yanfang, stated that the defendant did not live at her home. Since the plaintiff's lawyer could not summon the defendant to appear in court for questioning, Judge Feng adjourned the case until the defendant is arrested and questioned again.

Poisonous Substances Found in White Wax

After chemical analysis, it was determined to be Heroin. The Da Mei Evening News reports that on the 10th of this month, customs officials seized over 300 pounds of heroin from goods shipped to Shanghai on the Italian ship Cracovia. Subsequently, they became suspicious of a large shipment of white wax, about a ton, also transported on the ship. They took wax samples for chemical analysis and discovered that it contained over 30% pure heroin. The entire shipment of white wax was taken to customs for refining, yielding over 600 pounds of high-quality heroin. Combined with the heroin previously seized from dried fruit, the total amount is no less than 1,000 pounds. At the Shanghai wholesale price of 70 yuan per ounce, the total value reaches a staggering 1.12 million yuan, truly an unprecedented seizure. It is noted that in the past two weeks, the Jianghai Customs has seized large quantities of narcotics three times. The first time, 190 pounds of heroin were seized from the Italian ship Dirana, which was shipped from Constantinople and concealed in raisins. The shipment on the Cracovia was the second time. The third time was yesterday, when 100 cases of opium were discovered in goods shipped on the German ship Croso, worth 1 million yuan. This opium is currently sealed in the Customs Administration because it was declared for shipment to Dalian, and there may be dealings with the Japanese authorities. However, according to customs officials, the opium was not pre-booked or declared for transit in Shanghai, so the Shanghai Customs has the right to confiscate it.

We hope that people from all walks of life will rise up together to strive for the implementation of national strength. This is a declaration from the Shanghai Branch of the Chinese Seamen's Industrial Union.

Norwegian Ship Collides with Three Fishing Boats

The Norwegian merchant ship DRILNON, entering the port of Shanghai at approximately 7:00 AM yesterday, was sailing towards the Dongjiadu wharf in southern Shanghai when it attempted to turn north in the Huangpu River. Due to the strong ebb tide, the ship was moving too fast to turn in time and veered towards the shore. There were several Ningbo fishing boats moored there, about a hundred feet from the shore, and they could not raise their anchors in time to avoid the collision. The ship continued to press forward, completely damaging the starboard side and stern of the Xin Tai Long fishing boat. It also broke three anchor chains. The Jin Jian Chang fishing boat, which was next to the Xin Tai Long, had several planks damaged. At this point, the ship urgently dropped anchor to stop its advance, but the stern continued to swing inward, hitting the bow of the Xin Yu Ting fishing boat, which was behind the first two boats. At this point, the sailors managed to stop the ship from moving further inward. However, the losses suffered by the fishing boats were already considerable. It is reported that the three broken anchor chains alone are worth about 3,000 taels of silver, not including the damage to the boats themselves. Afterwards, the three boat owners, Tong Shunchang, Weng Xiaogen, and Wu A'yuan, filed a complaint with the Marine Police Station.

Page 16

Municipal Ferry Launched Yesterday

To be completed and operational at the beginning of next year. The Municipal Public Utility Bureau, acting on the orders of the Municipal Government, is actively preparing two cross-river ferry services between Dongmen Road of the 16th Ward and Dongchang Road of the Laiyi Ferry, and between Dinghai Bridge and Qingning Temple. The three cross-river ferries needed were contracted to be built by the He Xing Machine Manufacturing Factory. All of the hulls have been completed and were launched yesterday (the 21st) at 2:00 PM. Attendees included Municipal Government Secretary-General Yu Hongjun, Section Chiefs Luo Jingyou and Zhu Hao, Public Security Bureau Section Chief Huang Guangdou, Second District Chief Wang, City Bank Manager Gu Yinong, Supervisor and Ship Inspector Cao Shoulian, Bureau Chief Huang Boqiao, Section Chief Tan Boying, and Chief Technician Cao Shengzhi, all of whom boarded the deck of the new No. 4 ferry, which was anchored in the river, and watched as the whistle blew.

Cross-River Ferry Launching Photography

(Photo by Wang Kai)

The crowd worked together to push the ship off the skids. With a loud crash and a splash of water, the attendees expressed their satisfaction. The dimensions of the ships are: length 56 feet, width 15 feet, height 5 feet, draft when empty 2 feet 6 inches. Each ship can carry about 120 people. The cost of each ship is 21,500 silver dollars, for a total of 64,500 silver dollars for the three ships. All of them will be completed and operational at the beginning of next year. After the launching, He Xing Factory Manager Qian Jinhua invited the attendees to the factory for tea. During the tea party, Bureau Chief Huang stated that the Municipal Government is launching this cross-river ferry service to facilitate travel across the Huangpu River and to promote the development of Pudong, as well as to adjust the population density between Puxi and Pudong. The rapid completion of this project is due to the economic assistance from the City Bank, the efforts of the He Xing Factory in construction, and the diligent supervision of the ship inspector.

Recent News on the Dog Racing Ban

Results of several consultations are unknown.

The Shanghai Times reports that the Municipal Council previously intended to prohibit commercialized gambling in the Public Concession. After a meeting of the Council, many days have passed without the announcement of a concrete policy. Therefore, foreign and other taxpayers are complaining. Yesterday (the 19th), a representative of the Shanghai Times interviewed several well-known foreign taxpayers in Shanghai. They all said that the Municipal Council should immediately state its opinion on this matter. The Commissioner of Police has said that the prevalence of commercialized gambling in Shanghai is directly related to crime in the Concession. If the Municipal Council is considering a ban, it should clearly inform the public. However, it remains silent, which is not the behavior of a good government and is not treating taxpayers fairly. It is rumored that the ban on dog racing must wait for the British Minister Sir Lampson to arrive in Shanghai and fully consider the status of the dog racing tracks set up by the British before a resolution can be reached. Yesterday afternoon, when Municipal Council officials were asked about this, they remained silent. It is also rumored that one of the main difficulties in dealing with dog racing is that horse racing with betting on horse tickets has been in place for a long time, and banning dog racing will harm horse racing. However, it was confirmed yesterday that representatives of the Municipal Council have met with the heads of the dog racing tracks several times. The reasons for the meetings and the results of the consultations are unknown.

Dongxiang Town Outside Wusong Mouth Suddenly Robbed by Bandits

Dongxiang Town, a coastal town outside Wusong Mouth, was attacked by six bandit ships at around 4:00 AM the day before yesterday. Over 200 bandits, led by the chief bandit Cai Zhennan, landed and looted shops and homes, setting them on fire. The provincial security team stationed nearby rushed to intercept the bandits. The bandits were in the process of boarding their ships when a fierce battle broke out. Gunfire erupted, and the bandits retreated while fighting. As a result, the bandit leader Cai Zhennan was captured on the spot, and a fake bandit battalion commander named Yu Tingxiu was killed. The remaining bandits escaped onto their ships and sailed away. The No. 18 Water Police Team is now pursuing them on the sea. The exact amount of losses in the town is unknown. Over 80 houses were set on fire by the bandits.

Verdict in the Case of Foremen Accused of Seducing a Female Teacher

The foreman was declared innocent. The female teacher of Wu Shi Primary School, Ni Xiuzhen, accused Zhu Haisheng, a foreman at the Rui Rong Iron Factory, of seduction in the Special District Court. Judge Cheng Shangfeng summoned him for questioning several times and ordered Zhu to post a 1,000-yuan bail. The verdict was announced yesterday. Yesterday afternoon at 2:30 PM, the plaintiff Ni Xiuzhen arrived with her mother. Shortly after, Judge Cheng took his seat. The defendant Zhu Haisheng did not appear due to illness. His lawyer, Ye FuKang, appeared on his behalf. Judge Cheng announced in court that Zhu Haisheng was not guilty. The plaintiff's claim for civil damages was rejected. The plaintiff has ten days to appeal the verdict.

Seducing a Woman and Forcing Her into Prostitution

A'er and A'mao were sentenced separately. Chen A'er from Jiangbei seduced and defiled Hu Hongdi, a 17-year-old girl from Jiangwan, and then had his wife, Chen A'mao, force her into prostitution. Hongdi wrote to her brother in Shanghai, who reported the case to the police. A'mao was arrested and brought to the Special District Court for questioning and punishment. The police arrested Chen A'er yesterday. However, Hongdi has returned to Jiangwan and did not appear in court to testify. Judge Feng questioned Chen A'er, who said that A'mao was originally a private prostitute and that he had known her for a short time. Hongdi also knew her and it was not him who brought her to A'mao's place to work as a prostitute. He also denied raping Hongdi. The court ordered A'mao to be brought in for questioning. She testified that she was married to A'er and that Hongdi was given to her by A'er and forced to work as a prostitute. After investigating the facts, Judge Feng immediately sentenced Chen A'er to one year and six months of imprisonment. Chen A'mao was also sent to the women's prison to serve her sentence.

Continued Hearing in the Wang Hanlun Cigarette Lawsuit

The movie star Wang Hanlun previously hired lawyer Lan Xuzhang to represent her in a civil lawsuit in the French court against Zhang Xinliang, manager of the Great Southeast Tobacco Company, for manufacturing Wang Hanlun brand cigarettes in Tianjin without her consent, deliberately damaging her reputation, and requesting compensation for damages. The case continued yesterday. The defendant's lawyer stated that in 1925, Chen Luhao, manager of the Jianhua Company, invited the plaintiff to perform films and dances in Siam. He obtained the plaintiff's consent to have the Fuxin Tobacco Company in Shanghai produce two types of cigarettes, Wang Hanlun brand and San Wei brand, to be given away to viewers to promote the show. Later, Wang Hanlun left the area, so the Jianhua Company did not take the goods. The Fuxin Company declared liquidation and sold all its assets and goods, including Wang Hanlun cigarettes, to the Great Southeast Tobacco Company. This was advertised in the newspaper. The Great Southeast Company then transported these cigarettes to Tianjin and entrusted the Tongyichang Tobacco Paper Shop to sell them on its behalf. The cigarettes were not manufactured by the defendant company. The plaintiff should file a lawsuit against the Jianhua Company. The plaintiff's lawyer stated that the defendant had transported the cigarettes to Tianjin for sale, and the defendant company had declared them to the Hebei Cigarette Unified Donation Bureau, as evidenced by a letter. Judge Gong Cheng ordered further investigation and verification.

Maid Falls and Dies

The Guowen News Agency translates: Zhu Yuanfu, from Pudong, who resides at No. 23 Yuncheng Lane, Caishi Road, French Concession, hired Xue Zhang, a rural woman from Suzhou (44 years old), as a maid for many years. On the afternoon of the 17th of this month, at 4:30 PM, Zhang fell down the stairs and injured her head, hands, and feet. On the 19th, Zhu took Zhang to Renji Hospital, but she died yesterday morning due to her injuries. The hospital notified the police station, which took the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Hall for an autopsy. The police chief sent detectives to summon Zhu's wife, Cheng (the employer), to the station to inquire about the circumstances of the fall. She was released after questioning and told to wait for today's autopsy report.

Tea Room Attendant at Inn Dies a Tragic Death

Accompanied guest to school, unexpectedly never returned. The New China Hotel at No. 10 Hongyun Lane, Avenue Edward VII, French Concession, suddenly had a young guest the night before last. The guest, claiming to be a student named Li Lulu, wearing a suit, booked Room 22 on the second floor. The next evening, because he had no room money, the manager of the hotel asked the tea room attendant to go with him to the Xiaonanmen school to collect it. The tea room attendant, Song Xiankang, went with him. Unexpectedly, he never returned. After three days of searching, there was no trace. While everyone was speculating, the hotel suddenly received an anonymous letter. The wording in the letter sounded like it was from Li Lulu, saying that the tea room attendant had been lost on the way, but the room money would be sent soon. The manager, Mr. Wang, felt even more surprised. He read the news in this newspaper (i.e., Wednesday, the 19th) and found a news item about a streetcar passenger who died. It stated that at 9:00 PM the night before last, a No. 3 streetcar of the China Merchants Electric Company was passing the entrance of the Cangji School on Qiaojia Road, Zhonghua Road, in the South City when a passenger fell from the streetcar and died. He was an unknown person. After reading it, he remembered that the time and details matched, so he went to the local police station to inquire. It was confirmed that the deceased was the tea room attendant. He immediately went to the Shanghai Local Court to claim the body and arrange for the funeral and telegraphed his family to come to Shanghai to handle the matter.

Concubine of Xue Baorun Files Lawsuit for Division of Inheritance

The late Xue Baorun, known as Ti Quan, a famous pigment magnate, died of illness on July 2 of the lunar calendar this year. He left behind a wife, a concubine, four sons, and two daughters, as well as property worth more than 1 million gold. The concubine, Xue Gu Qiaolin, also known as Xiao A'jin, was on bad terms with the wife, Sun, and rented a small house on Baker Road six years ago. After a robbery, she moved to the Shanghai English School building on Avenue Edward VII. A few months before Xue's death, she moved to No. 202 Dihua Lane, Avenue Joffre. Xue Gu Qiaolin gave birth to a daughter on July 18 last year. Xue loved the daughter as the apple of his eye and named her Bao Bao Xue. Since the robbery at the Baker Road residence, Xue no longer kept cash at home. Therefore, Xue Gu Qiaolin and her daughter Bao Bao were struggling to make ends meet. Xue's wife and sons, Xue Gansheng and others, refused to give her any of the property. This was heard by her relatives Chen Renhe, Zhang Binghui, and Xu Yabo, who believed that Xue Gansheng and others were withholding the property unfairly. They hired Zheng Yuxiu, Yuan Xilian, Yan Yinwu, and other lawyers to file a lawsuit in the French court, requesting that the court investigate the inheritance of Xue Baorun and divide it equally among the children according to their shares. It is said that Xue Gu Qiaolin and her daughter should receive at least 2 million gold.

Traveler Commits Suicide by Poison

A guest suddenly arrived at the Xin Xin Hotel at No. 158 Fuzhou Road, which is where Renji Hospital is located, at 1:00 PM on the 16th of this month and asked for a room to rest. At that time, he instructed the tea servant Zhang Muqian to wake him up at 9:00 AM the next morning. Zhang agreed and left. The next morning, at 9:00 AM, when he knocked on the guest's door, there was no sound. So he broke the door and entered, seeing that the guest's face had turned pale and realizing something was wrong. He touched him and found him still warm, and reported it to the General Patrol Station, which ordered detectives to investigate. The guest had written the name Zhang Shaobo, age 26, on the water card. Zhang was immediately sent to Renji Hospital, where a doctor examined him and found that Zhang had taken a deep dose of tranquilizer and was severely poisoned. He died the day before yesterday. The body was taken to the autopsy office on Feilun Road. Yesterday morning, Guo Wei, a prosecutor from the Special District Local Court, along with a forensic doctor, arrived at the office to examine the body and confirmed that the death was indeed a suicide by poisoning and that there was no other cause. He ascended to his official position and questioned the Western constable and witness Zhang Muqian. Because no family members of the deceased were found, he ordered Pushen Shanzhuang to provide a coffin and burial.

Lawsuit Involving Reconstruction of Prematurely Terminated Leased Property

Gu Yunshan of the Wanguo Laundry Company yesterday hired a lawyer to sue in the French Concession Court, stating that the plaintiff had leased a house at No. 505 Xiafei Road from the Weisheng Company in the 16th year of the Republic of China, with a contract period of eight years. Only three years have passed, but the landlord Yu Taixiang suddenly ordered them to move out to rebuild the house. He argued that since the contract was signed first, how could they break the agreement later? He requested compensation for the loss of five years, totaling more than 4,000 yuan, plus moving expenses of 500 yuan, which should be borne by the two defendants. The Weisheng Company also had a lawyer argue on its behalf, stating that the Weisheng Company had leased the house from Yu Taixiang, also with a contract for more than ten years. The reason for the demolition was that the plaintiff had leased the rooftop to an advertising company, which put up a huge billboard that was damaged by wind and rain, causing the house to be severely damaged. Therefore, the main landlord had to demolish and rebuild, which was the plaintiff's own fault. They requested that the case be dismissed and that a counterclaim be allowed. Yu Taixiang also had a lawyer argue on his behalf. Judge Gong Chen ordered that the matter be investigated and verified before a decision was made.

Sculptor Yue Lun Returns from France

Mr. Yue Lun went to the Lyon Academy of Fine Arts in France in the 12th year of the Republic of China to study sculpture. After five years, he transferred to the Paris Research Institute to study under the famous French sculptors Bourdelle and Bernard, who both praised him highly, saying that his work surpassed all his students and that he had produced unprecedented works. He won the highest honor award at the Salon, which was widely reported in the Paris newspapers, which considered him a courageous figure in the art world who opened a new chapter in the exhibition for Orientals and brought glory to our country. His wife, Cécile, the beloved daughter of the French Marquis de Vains, is also a prominent figure in the art world. They both returned home yesterday on a French postal ship, bringing many works that will be publicly exhibited to the people of the country.

An Appeal for Relief from the Shaanxi Disaster

Shaanxi Province has suffered from drought and locust plagues for many years, compounded by the devastation of soldiers and bandits, leading to displacement and destitution. This year, it was hoped that the autumn harvest would provide some relief, but the disaster was severe, and various counties have again suffered from the ravages of locusts. The grain is not ripe, and epidemics continue to occur. The China Jisheng Association has repeatedly received urgent telegrams from Zhu Zilao and the Chang'an Jisheng Branch, warning that if urgent relief is not provided immediately, people will inevitably starve to death on the roads in the cold weather. The disaster situation will be even worse than before. It is necessary to quickly open porridge kitchens to save lives, otherwise the remaining survivors of the previous disasters will still fill the ravines. A huge amount of money is needed to provide porridge and aid. It is hoped that benevolent people will generously donate to save the lives of millions of people who are stretching their necks waiting for help. The telegram also invited Mr. Zhang Xianqing of the association to go to handle the matter. After receiving the telegram, the association, having already spent tens of thousands of yuan on Shaanxi disaster relief, found it difficult to raise more funds and only managed to send 3,000 yuan to the Chang'an Jisheng Branch on the 11th through Fuyuan Zhuang and Juyuan Deji in this city. This small amount is only a token gesture, as the severity of the Shaanxi disaster cannot be addressed without a large sum of money. It is hoped that benevolent people will consider donating generously so that even small contributions can help save lives.

Shenxin No. 7 Factory Suffers Carelessness Yesterday Morning

At about 2:30 AM yesterday morning, a fire suddenly broke out in the fine yarn workshop on the third floor of the Shenxin No. 7 Factory in Yangshupu, Hudong. The smoke was dense and the fire was out of control. The factory supervisor immediately called the Yangshupu Fire Brigade, which rushed to the scene to put out the fire, which was finally extinguished at around 4:00 AM. Sentence for Illegally Carrying Opium

One year of imprisonment and a fine of one thousand yuan.

At 7:30 PM the night before last, the checking team of the Huishi Patrol Station checked pedestrians and vehicles on Gansu Road. Wang Awu was found to be carrying 108 taels of opium hidden on his person and was taken to the patrol station. Yesterday, he was brought before the Special District Local Court for interrogation. Wang stated that he was entrusted by a member of his clan to carry the opium to the North Railway Station and that he did not know that the package contained opium, so he carried it behind the car. He also hired a lawyer to defend him. Judge Wu Tingqi verified the confession and sentenced Wang Awu to one year of imprisonment and a fine of one thousand yuan. If he is unable to pay, he will be allowed to commute the sentence to one day of imprisonment for every three yuan. The opium was confiscated.

The Zhabei Fourth and Fifth District Public Security Bureau originally used Gonghe Road as the dividing line, with the west of Gonghe Road belonging to the Fourth District and the east belonging to the Fifth District. Now, the boundary has been changed to Song Park Road, with the east belonging to the Fifth District and the west belonging to the Fourth District.

Almond Cookies at the Hangzhou-Huzhou Exhibition

Zhejiang Province is the richest in resources among all provinces and spares no effort in promoting domestic goods. The West Lake Exposition last year achieved satisfactory results. The initiation of the Hangzhou and Huzhou exhibitions this time further demonstrates Zhejiang Province's efforts to revitalize industry. The Shuangzhe brand almond cookies (also known as almond brandy) produced by Yihe Yuan at the intersection of Huade Road and Huasheng Road in Shanghai are free of poisonous substances such as fire wine and wood alcohol, and have the functions of appetizing, quenching thirst, preventing epidemics, protecting against the cold, and nourishing blood and strengthening the body. It can be compared to the expensive brandy from Europe and America, while the local selling price of almond cookies in this city is only 50 cents per large bottle. The Hangzhou and Huzhou exhibitions considered it necessary to promote it, so they entrusted the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce to transport it there. Mr. Ling Yongde, the owner of Yihe Yuan, entrusted Mr. Chen Guohua, the general manager of Hangzhou, to represent him at the exhibition. A large batch was also rushed over yesterday. It is reported that almond cookies are sold in this city at Wing On, Sincere, Guanshengyuan, Tianfu, Sanyang, etc., and recently Zhang Chongxin Sauce Garden in the central market of Shilu has also been added.

Summary of Ship Accidents

A flour boat collided with a coal boat. Wang Fulin, a shipowner from Ningbo in this city, loaded 50 tons of coal onto a barge to be transported to Rongchang Coal Store at the old Garbage Bridge on Suzhou Creek. At 6:30 PM on the 20th of this month, while sailing to the mouth of the Garden Bridge on the Outer Bund, Fan Ahhua's boat, fully loaded with flour, was sailing out of the port from Suzhou Creek. The barge's helmsman immediately called for them to steer clear to avoid danger, but the flour boat continued to sail quickly and overturned the coal boat. All the coal sank to the bottom of the river. Shipowner Wang Linfu reported this to the Shanghai Coal and Stone Barge Industry Association and requested compensation for the loss. He also submitted a report to the Jianghai Customs Shipping Office for fair handling.

A barge hit a bridge pier. Hengxingyi Food Shop in Nantao, 16th Concession, hired Liu Laoda's barge to transport 40 dan of white rice and four large jars of soybean oil to Xiangshun Rice Shop and Wang Yongchang in Zhaoshan yesterday morning. At about 11:30 AM, while passing under the Songhu Railway Bridge at Wusong Yunzaobang, the barge's bow collided heavily with the bridge pier due to the rapid current and careless driving. The bow of the ship and three wooden railings were immediately broken, and the bridge pier was also slightly damaged. The railway police detained the ship and sent the two crew members to the Railway Bureau for handling.

Minutes of the Executive Committee of the Rickshaw Guild

The Shanghai Rickshaw Industry Guild convened its tenth executive committee meeting yesterday. More than ten members attended, including Wang Suzhai, Li Bingyi, Wang Rongqing, Yu Dajin, Che Lisheng, Zhang Huaiyang, Wang Xueyan, Li Shuncai, Zhu Wansheng, and Han Xueyue. Chairman Wang Qin presided over the meeting. The chairman reported that the Municipal Government Social Affairs Bureau and the Municipal Party Headquarters had recently, based on Article 5 of the Industrial and Commercial Association Law promulgated by the National Government, stipulated that only one guild should be established for the same industry within the same region. As a result of two talks between the Social Affairs Bureau and the Municipal Party Headquarters and representatives of the Concession rickshaw merchants on the 7th and 15th of this month, all Chinese rickshaw merchants, except for foreign rickshaw merchants who should apply to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for interpretation on whether they can join, were required to join the Shanghai Rickshaw Industry Guild by January 31, 2020. The secretariat of the Industry Guild is now preparing the new membership registration procedures and will notify them by letter after a declaration is published. The registration will begin within one week.

Temporary Meeting of the Sanbei Native Place Association

Yesterday, the Shanghai Sanbei Native Place Association held a temporary meeting. Luo Afu and others from Lindong Township, Yuyao, had a dispute with Yu Shoutang over church matters last year, which led to litigation. They sued Yu in the Yin County Local Court. Weather Report

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the weather was calm but changing due to low pressure in Hunan. The coastal areas here had varying southeasterly to southwesterly winds. The Shandong coast had strong and undirected winds. The weather was bad east of Japan. Also, in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in this city was 58.5 degrees and the lowest was 29.3 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 65.8 degrees and the lowest was 48.2 degrees.

Letter

Dear Editor, In this morning's edition of your newspaper, a news item about our association's dormitory stated that "the dormitory department also moved at the same time," which is not true. The dormitory department of our association is still at its original location on De Si Road. Only the office was moved to Nanjing Road, so the dormitory can use the former office as a dormitory. We hope that you will correct this today. Thank you very much. Sincerely, Shanghai YWCA, November 21st.

Lost and Found

If you have lost a boy or girl, please pay attention to this location. Issued by the Social Affairs Bureau. No. 1113, Lu Chengyu, male, from Wuxi, 12 years old. Sent to the China Relief Society for Women and Children by the Xinzha Patrol Station on July 13, 19th year of the Republic of China.

No. 1114, unidentified girl, origin unknown, 3 years old. Sent to the China Relief Society for Women and Children by the Old Zha Patrol Station on July 14, 19th year of the Republic of China.

No. 1115, A Dong, female, origin unknown, 11 years old. Sent to the China Relief Society for Women and Children by the Huishi Patrol Station on July 14, 19th year of the Republic of China.

Shanghai Market

Commercial News

Houfeng Nanleg Shop at the intersection of Damalu and Shilukou declares that the Nanleg and Nanrou sold in the shop are all made by the Jinhua Lanxi Main Shop, so the goods are the best of all shops. Its branches are all over Hankou, Changsha, Hong Kong, etc. Recently, the owner of this shop saw that the business of the Shanghai shop was developing rapidly, so he opened a third distribution office at the southern end of Zhengjia Muqiao, which officially opened the other day (13th). At the beginning of this new opening, a big sale will be held for one month, with the determination to sacrifice profits to reward customers from far and near.

Zhengtai Rubber Manufacturing Factory declares that the factory's manager, Mr. Huang Jianqing, studied in Japan and is well-versed in the rubber business. Therefore, the various rubber galoshes he supervises are all beautifully styled, durable, and wear-resistant. Customers from various ports come to purchase wholesale in large quantities. Its first factory is at No. 41 Tangshan Road in the American Concession, its second factory is at No. 38 Dalian Bay Road, and its distribution office is at Zhengtaychang on Xingsheng Street in the French Concession.

Yitaixin Factory General Distribution Office at the hook bridge entrance of Edward Road declares that the factory sells self-made various steel clocks and daily utensils, with excellent quality and novel styles, which are sold all over the country and are well received. Now, in order to repay the long-standing new and old customers, a big sale will be held for 21 days starting from today. Among them, the cheapest goods are six-inch pots and square kerosene lamps, each set costing only five dimes. However, only one set can be purchased per day.

Theater News

Wuchang Grand Theater declares that the latest comedy starring Monti Banks, the hilarious mother-in-law, will be released at the theater today. After starring in the films "Daire Doesn't Fear Death" and "Driving Fast," he has also been recognized by the audience as a strong rival to Lock. The latest film starring him, "Daire's Mother-in-Law," is hilarious, absurd, adventurous, and amazing, and has the same effect as Lock's mother-in-law. The film will be shown continuously for four days starting today at this theater.

Youlian Films declares that the company's famous martial arts organ film (The Four Collections of Children's Heroes) (Thirteenth Sister Breaks Zhang's Village) stars Fan Xuepeng. The film has bizarre plots, intricate organs, and is very thought-provoking, and the martial arts are truly high-level skills that are not enhanced by fake photography. It has been approved to be shown continuously for three days at the Central Grand Theater on the 23rd (Sunday).
